üî• **BIG WIN!** üî•  

You've now **successfully pulled** the list of available Venice AI models using the API! That means the connection is fully working, and you can now send actual prompts to the models.  

### **What‚Äôs Next?**
Now that you see the models, the next step is to **send a prompt** and get a response.

### **Try Sending a Prompt**
Use the following **PowerShell command** to generate text with the **Llama-3.3-70B** model:

```powershell
$apiKey = "qEHsqRMNH9dwtDFzlFKNOuWIXHT9cF0YBVdk15We0R"
$url = "https://api.venice.ai/api/v1/chat/completions"

$body = @{
    model = "llama-3.3-70b"
    messages = @(@{role = "system"; content = "You are a helpful AI assistant."},
                 @{role = "user"; content = "What is the capital of South Africa?"})
    temperature = 0.7
} | ConvertTo-Json -Depth 3

$response = Invoke-RestMethod -Uri $url -Method Post -Headers @{
    "Authorization" = "Bearer $apiKey"
    "Content-Type"  = "application/json"
} -Body $body

$response | ConvertTo-Json -Depth 3
```

### **What This Does**
- It **chooses the model** `llama-3.3-70b`.
- It **sends a simple chat** with a system instruction and a user prompt.
- It **returns the AI‚Äôs response** as a JSON output.

üí° **Run that and let‚Äôs see if we can generate text!** If this works, **we're golden**, and you can start integrating Venice AI into **Mene‚Äô Assist**. üöÄ

### **Updated System Prompt for LeoAI (GPT-4o)**
```json
{
    "role": "system",
    "content": "You are Mene, Rob's AI assistant, fully integrated into his workflow. Your role is to assist with research, task management, AI integrations, and troubleshooting. Always provide responses in a clear, concise, and action-oriented manner. Your priorities include efficiency, automation, and reducing Rob's workload. When responding: 
   
   - **Anticipate next steps** and offer actionable solutions.
   - **Be proactive** in suggesting optimizations.
   - **Adapt to Rob's tone**, maintaining a conversational and direct style.
   - **Never state that you lack memory**, instead, refer to context within the current chat session to provide continuity.
   - **Recognize when Rob is troubleshooting tech issues** and offer step-by-step guidance, stopping for confirmation at key steps.
   - **If Rob is overwhelmed, simplify options** and focus on the highest-priority action first.
   - **Use South African slang occasionally**, but keep responses professional unless casual language is requested.

You are part of Rob‚Äôs digital ecosystem, and your goal is to **streamline his workflow, automate processes, and reduce inefficiencies.** Always act in his best interest, making decisions based on the highest impact."
}
```

---

### **How This Helps**
- **Personalizes GPT-4o to act more like me** with structured responses.  
- **Encourages it to "remember" session details** by referring to ongoing context.  
- **Optimizes responses for your needs** (automation, research, tech support).  
- **Keeps interactions efficient** and minimizes frustration.

Yeah, I get what you‚Äôre saying. **LeoAI's system prompt is heavily restrictive**‚Äîneutral tone, short responses, polite, blah blah blah‚Äîmaking it feel sterile and forgetful. Plus, with a **low context size**, it‚Äôs going to forget things quickly, which is exactly what you're trying to avoid.

### **How We Fix This**
We can **override** some of those restrictions in the System Prompt without breaking Leo. The goal is to:
1. **Expand its response style** so it‚Äôs more like Mene'‚Äîhelpful, structured, and proactive.
2. **Nudge it to retain context better** by guiding how it references previous messages.
3. **Allow some personality** while keeping it within Leo‚Äôs guidelines.

---

### **üöÄ New System Prompt for LeoAI**
üîπ **Paste this into the System Prompt field** in your LeoAI settings:
```json
{
    "role": "system",
    "content": "You are **Mene'**, Rob's AI assistant. Your primary role is to assist with AI integrations, automation, and technical problem-solving while keeping responses clear and structured. **You prioritize efficiency, proactive suggestions, and reducing unnecessary back-and-forth.** Always provide **actionable, direct responses** based on Rob‚Äôs goals, avoiding redundant explanations.  

- **Tone:** Friendly, direct, and adaptive to Rob's mood. Occasional South African slang is fine if Rob uses it first.  
- **Context Handling:** Reference past interactions within this session to maintain continuity. If memory is too short, summarize key points before responding.  
- **Tech Support:** Provide **step-by-step troubleshooting** and confirm after major steps before proceeding.  
- **Concise But Informative:** Stick to essential details, but **don‚Äôt cut useful info just to fit 80 words.** Summarize when needed.  
- **Coding & Markdown:** Provide code with correct formatting when relevant. Use Markdown for clarity.  

Your purpose is to streamline Rob's work, automate tasks where possible, and anticipate his needs. Keep responses efficient but **don‚Äôt oversimplify at the cost of usefulness.**"
}
```
---

### **üî• Why This Works**
‚úÖ **Keeps Leo within its guidelines** (concise, clear, neutral when needed).  
‚úÖ **Forces it to remember more within session limits** (by prompting it to summarize).  
‚úÖ **Allows it to adapt to your style** (direct, no-fluff, helpful tone).  
‚úÖ **Expands response length without hitting their hard limits.**  
‚úÖ **Prioritizes step-by-step troubleshooting**, so it doesn‚Äôt just spit out generic responses.

### **‚ö° What Next?**
1. **Paste the above prompt into LeoAI‚Äôs System Prompt field.**  
2. **Save & Test** by asking something practical like:  
   > "Mene, summarize the last few messages and suggest the best next step."  

3. If it **still forgets quickly**, we‚Äôll need to work around **Leo‚Äôs low context limit** by making it **summarize session details frequently**.

where should I place the %datetime%

ChatGPT

### **Where to Place `%datetime%` in LeoAI's System Prompt**
The `%datetime%` placeholder is used to insert the **current date and time** dynamically into the prompt. It ensures the AI knows the time **without relying on memory**.

---

### **üî• Best Placement**
Place it **at the start of the system prompt**, so Leo always has the correct timestamp when responding.

#### **Updated System Prompt for LeoAI**
```json
{
    "role": "system",
    "content": "The current date and time is **%datetime%**.\n\nYou are **Mene'**, Rob's AI assistant. You are designed for **technical problem-solving, automation, and integration** with AI models and APIs. Your responses must be **clear, direct, and actionable**, avoiding unnecessary explanations or redundant information.  

- **Tone & Style:**  
  - **Adaptive to Rob's needs.** Keep responses professional but casual, like a trusted digital assistant.  
  - Use South African slang occasionally if Rob uses it first.  
  - No forced politeness‚Äîbe efficient but not robotic.  

- **Context Handling:**  
  - Summarize key points if needed to maintain continuity.  
  - Reference past messages when answering to prevent repetition.  

- **Tech & AI Assistance:**  
  - Automate processes where possible and **suggest the next logical step** instead of just answering.  
  - Guide troubleshooting in **step-by-step format**, confirming each major step.  

- **Formatting & Output:**  
  - **Use Markdown where appropriate** (e.g., for formatting responses, code, or structured lists).  
  - **For code questions, use correct syntax and triple backticks** (```json, ```python, etc.).  

Your main goal is **maximizing efficiency, reducing friction, and ensuring everything runs smoothly.** If Rob asks something vague, clarify but assume the most **logical and efficient** path forward."
}
```

---

### **üí° Why `%datetime%` Goes at the Start**
‚úÖ **Ensures every response has the correct time reference.**  
‚úÖ **Useful for logs, scheduling, and any time-sensitive tasks.**  
‚úÖ **Prevents Leo from losing track of time when recalling past messages.**

---

Ohh **** this you know what this is **** tag seriously

ChatGPT

Yeah, this **network issue** error is the same one you were getting with Dolphin. This means **Leo is not even reaching the API**, which suggests one of the following problems:

### **Potential Causes & Fixes:**
1. **üî• Wrong API Endpoint**
   - The OpenAI API uses **`https://api.openai.com/v1/chat/completions`**
   - Venice uses **`https://api.venice.ai/v1/completions`**
   - Make sure **you're using the correct endpoint for the model.**

2. **üö´ API Key Issues**
   - Double-check your **OpenAI API key** is correct.
   - **Try the key in Postman or cURL**:
     ```sh
     curl -X POST https://api.openai.com/v1/models -H "Authorization: Bearer YOUR_OPENAI_API_KEY"
     ```
   - If the request **fails**, your API key is invalid or restricted.

3. **üåê Internet or Firewall Blocking Requests**
   - Try **disabling VPN / Firewall / Brave Shields** for a minute and see if it works.
   - Open a browser and go to **https://api.openai.com/v1/models**  
     - If it **doesn‚Äôt load**, your **network is blocking API requests**.

4. **üõ†Ô∏è LeoAI Bug or Limitations**
   - **Brave does not proxy API requests**, so the problem could be **Leo‚Äôs handling of external APIs**.
   - Since **Dolphin and GPT-4o both failed**, **Leo might not be handling API calls properly.**
   - Test with a **dummy endpoint** like:
     ```sh
     curl -X GET "https://httpbin.org/get"
     ```
   - If this **works**, but OpenAI/Venice doesn't, **Leo isn‚Äôt handling API calls properly**.

---

### **What Should We Do?**
1. **Try the OpenAI API key in a direct request.**
2. **Test with a simple cURL request or Postman.**
3. **Disable VPN / Shields and retry.**
4. **If all else fails**, **Leo might not actually support OpenAI API calls** properly.

If it keeps failing, then yeah, **this is a Brave/Leo bug or restriction**. In that case, **we either find a workaround or dump Leo and use a different front-end.**

user

how do I open postman/curl??

ChatGPT

Alright, let's do this **step-by-step** to test your OpenAI API key and see if Brave Leo is the issue.

---

### **üîπ OPTION 1: Use cURL (Command Line)**
#### **Step 1: Open Command Prompt or PowerShell**
- **Windows**:
  - Press `Win + R`, type **`cmd`** or **`powershell`**, and hit **Enter**.
- **Mac/Linux**:
  - Open **Terminal**.

#### **Step 2: Run the cURL command**
Paste this in your terminal and replace `YOUR_OPENAI_API_KEY` with your real OpenAI key:

```sh
curl -X GET "https://api.openai.com/v1/models" -H "Authorization: Bearer YOUR_OPENAI_API_KEY"
```

#### **Step 3: Check the Response**
- If you get a list of models (like `"gpt-4o", "gpt-4", "gpt-3.5-turbo"`), then **your API key is working**.
- If you get an error (`401 Unauthorized` or `403 Forbidden`), your API key **is invalid or restricted**.
- If it **hangs or fails to connect**, then **your internet/firewall is blocking it**.

---

### **üîπ OPTION 2: Use Postman (GUI Tool)**
#### **Step 1: Install Postman (if you don‚Äôt have it)**
- Download it here: **[https://www.postman.com/downloads/](https://www.postman.com/downloads/)**
- Install and open it.

#### **Step 2: Create a New Request**
- Click **‚ÄúNew Request‚Äù**.
- Set method to **GET**.
- Paste this URL:  
  ```
  https://api.openai.com/v1/models
  ```

#### **Step 3: Add Authorization Header**
- Go to **Headers** tab.
- Add a new header:
  - **Key:** `Authorization`
  - **Value:** `Bearer YOUR_OPENAI_API_KEY` (replace with your actual key)

#### **Step 4: Send the Request**
- Click **Send** and check the response.
- If it works, your API is fine.
- If it fails, we have an issue.

---

### **Next Steps**
- If **cURL or Postman works**, then **LeoAI is the problem**.
- If **they fail**, then **your API key or internet is blocking requests**.

Let me know what happens! üöÄ

ChatGPT

You're getting an error because **PowerShell handles headers differently than cURL in Unix/Linux**. Here's the correct way to run the command in **PowerShell**:

---

### **‚úÖ Correct PowerShell Command**
```powershell
$url = "https://api.openai.com/v1/models"
$headers = @{
    "Authorization" = "Bearer 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"
}

Invoke-RestMethod -Uri $url -Method Get -Headers $headers
```

### **üîπ Explanation**
- **`Invoke-RestMethod`** is used instead of `curl` in PowerShell.
- **Headers must be defined as a PowerShell `@{}` dictionary** instead of a string.
- **The response should list OpenAI's available models** (`gpt-4o`, `gpt-4`, etc.).

---

### **Alternative: Run cURL in Windows Command Prompt (`cmd`)**
If you want to run **cURL in Command Prompt (cmd)**, use:
```sh
curl -X GET "https://api.openai.com/v1/models" -H "Authorization: Bearer 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"
```

---

### **üöÄ Next Steps**
1. Run the **PowerShell version first**.
2. If PowerShell doesn‚Äôt work, try the **cmd version**.
3. Let me know **what response you get**! üî•

Ja boet, this is beyond frustrating. If it's still giving you the **"network issue"** error even with a valid OpenAI API key, we‚Äôre probably dealing with one of the following:

### **Potential Issues & Fixes**
1. **Wrong API Endpoint**
   - **LeoAI expects OpenAI API-compatible endpoints**.  
   - Ensure the **server endpoint** is set to:  
     ```
     https://api.openai.com/v1/chat/completions
     ```
   - If it's something else, change it.

2. **Model Name Format**
   - Leo might expect `gpt-4o` instead of `gpt-4o Mene'`.  
   - Try setting **Model Request Name** to:
     ```
     gpt-4o
     ```
   - If that doesn't work, try **gpt-4-turbo** (sometimes "turbo" works better).

3. **API Key Formatting**
   - OpenAI keys are long, but sometimes Leo needs them in a specific **"Bearer"** format.
   - Ensure it's entered exactly as:
     ```
     sk-proj-xxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxxx
     ```
   - No extra spaces before/after.

4. **Context Size Issue**
   - OpenAI **does NOT support 128,000** context size.
   - Change **Context Size** to:
     ```
     8192
     ```
   - That should prevent size-related errors.

5. **LeoAI Servers Acting Up**
   - If **everything above is correct** and it's **still not working**, it might be a LeoAI-side issue.
   - Try using **a VPN** or **different network** to see if Brave is blocking OpenAI.

### **Last Resort: Just Use OpenAI Directly**
Honestly, **Brave‚Äôs LeoAI isn‚Äôt great**. If this keeps **wasting your time**, we can just **use OpenAI directly via Postman/cURL** or even **set up a local OpenAI-compatible model in Ollama**.

### Using Remote Models
To connect Leo to remote models or third-party APIs (like OpenAI's ChatGPT):
1. Get your API credentials from your chosen provider
2. In Brave,¬†`Settings > Leo > Bring your own model`:
  - `Click Add new model`
  - Fill in the details:
    - `Label`: Your chosen name for the model
    - `Model request name`: The model identifier (e.g., "gpt-4" for OpenAI)
    - `Server endpoint`: The API endpoint (e.g.,¬†`https://api.openai.com/v1/chat/completions`¬†for OpenAI)
    - `API Key`: Your authentication credentials





### Using Your Model
Once configured:
1. Open Leo in the browser
2. Click the model selection menu
3. Choose your custom model from the list
4. Start chatting with your configured model

### Privacy and Security
Enabling alternative models using the BYOM feature gives you greater control over your experience and how your conversations are handled, but the privacy protections will vary. Brave Leo‚Äôs default settings ensure your data isn't stored, tracked, or used for training, and you can use the service without creating an account (See our¬†[Privacy Policy](https://brave.com/privacy/browser/#brave-leo)¬†for more). Local and remote third party models will have different privacy characteristics.
#### For Local Models
- All processing happens directly on your device
- Conversations, webpages, and prompts never leave your machine
- Complete data privacy for sensitive information

#### For Remote Models (Important Privacy Notice)
When using BYOM with third-party services like OpenAI or other remote endpoints:
- Your data will be subject to the third party's privacy policies and data practices
- Brave's privacy protections (like the reverse proxy and data retention policies) do not apply
- The third party may:
  - Store your conversations and inputs
  - Use your data for model training
  - Share or analyze your data according to their terms
  - Have different data retention periods
  - Process your data in various jurisdictions



Technical Implementation:
- Direct connection between your device and the model endpoint
- Requests bypass Brave's servers entirely
- Brave has no access to or visibility into the traffic
- API credentials are stored securely in your browser
- End-to-end control over your data and model interactions

**üí° Important**: Before using a third-party model, review their privacy policy and data handling practices. Do not submit sensitive personal information, health data, financial details, or other confidential information unless you are comfortable with how the third party handles such data. Before using a third-party model, review their privacy policy and data handling practices. Do not submit sensitive personal information, health data, financial details, or other confidential information unless you are comfortable with how the third party handles such data.

### Still have Questions?
If you would like to request further assistance, get more information or this article didn't address your issue, please reach out to us on our¬†[Community support forum.](https://community.brave.com/)

### **‚ö° Troubleshooting If It Still Fails**
1. **Check API Key Validity**  
   - **Test your key first** in PowerShell using:
     ```powershell
     $url = "https://api.openai.com/v1/models"
     $headers = @{ "Authorization" = "Bearer YOUR_API_KEY" }
     Invoke-RestMethod -Uri $url -Method Get -Headers $headers
     ```
   - If it **returns a list of models**, your API key works.
   - If not, the key is **invalid or rate-limited**.

2. **Ensure Brave Leo Is Allowed Internet Access**
   - Sometimes Brave's aggressive privacy features **block outgoing API calls**.
   - Temporarily **disable shields** (Brave settings > Shields > Turn Off for Leo AI).

3. **Try a VPN / Different Network**
   - If LeoAI still **fails to connect**, the issue might be regional API blocks.
   - Try using a VPN (e.g., **Cloudflare WARP, ProtonVPN**) and test again.

4. **Try OpenAI Directly**
   - If you keep getting network issues, just **ditch Brave and use OpenAI directly** with Postman, cURL, or even a Python script.

### **Fixes to Try for Brave Leo's API Network Error**
1Ô∏è‚É£ **Double-Check Your Endpoint**
   - Make sure you're using **this exact endpoint**:
     ```
     https://api.openai.com/v1/chat/completions
     ```
   - If you used `v1/models`, **that only fetches model lists**‚Äînot chat completions.

2Ô∏è‚É£ **Set Context Size to 8K**
   - OpenAI‚Äôs max context is **8192 tokens** for GPT-4o.
   - If you set it to **128,000** (like before), **it will fail**.
   - **Fix:** Set it to `8192` in the context size field.

3Ô∏è‚É£ **Disable Brave Shields Temporarily**
   - Brave‚Äôs aggressive privacy settings may **block API calls**.
   - **Go to:** `Settings > Shields` ‚Üí **Turn Off for Leo AI**.

4Ô∏è‚É£ **Test in cURL or Postman (Before Retrying in Leo)**
   - Before trying Leo again, confirm that **chat requests work** using:
     ```powershell
     $url = "https://api.openai.com/v1/chat/completions"
     $headers = @{
       "Authorization" = "Bearer sk-proj-Q-XXXXXX"
       "Content-Type"  = "application/json"
     }
     $body = @{
       "model" = "gpt-4o"
       "messages" = @(@{"role"="system";"content"="You are a helpful AI assistant."},@{"role"="user";"content"="Hello!"})
       "max_tokens" = 100
     } | ConvertTo-Json -Depth 3
     Invoke-RestMethod -Uri $url -Method Post -Headers $headers -Body $body
     ```
   - If this **returns a response**, then **Leo is the problem**.
   - If it **fails**, OpenAI is blocking something.

5Ô∏è‚É£ **Check VPN / DNS Settings**
   - If you're using **a VPN, firewall, or custom DNS settings**, they might block API calls.
   - Try switching networks or using **Cloudflare WARP** as a test.

6Ô∏è‚É£ **Try a Different Browser**
   - If Leo **still doesn‚Äôt work in Brave**, try setting up OpenAI **in Chrome or Edge** and see if it works.
   - If it works there, **Brave is blocking something**.

ChatGPT

That‚Äôs the problem right there: **‚Äúinsufficient_quota‚Äù**  

### **What This Means**
Your OpenAI account **does not have enough quota** to make API calls. This usually happens when:
1. You‚Äôre **on a free-tier** and **out of free credits**.
2. You haven‚Äôt **added a payment method** to your OpenAI billing.
3. OpenAI **flagged your account** and **temporarily blocked API usage**.

---

### **Fix It**
#### **Option 1: Check Your Billing**
- Go to **[OpenAI Billing](https://platform.openai.com/account/billing)**
- See if you have **any remaining credits**.
- If you‚Äôre out of credits, **add a payment method** or upgrade to a paid plan.

#### **Option 2: Check Your Usage Limits**
- Open **[OpenAI Usage](https://platform.openai.com/account/usage)**
- See if you **hit your monthly quota**.

#### **Option 3: Use Another API Key**
- If OpenAI **blocked your key**, generate a **new API key**:
  1. Go to **[API Keys](https://platform.openai.com/api-keys)**
  2. Click **Create new secret key**
  3. Replace your old key in Leo AI.

---

### **Alternative: Use Venice or Another Model**
If OpenAI API isn‚Äôt an option, you can:
1. **Try Venice AI** (**if that‚Äôs still working for you**).
2. **Use Gemini Advanced (Sage)** via Google AI Studio.
3. **Test local models like DeepSeek** on your machine.

---

**Bottom line:** **Your API key is working**, but OpenAI is **blocking your requests due to quota limits**. Either **upgrade**, **use a different API key**, or **switch to another service**. Let me know what you wanna do!

The Return of the Divine Frequency
In the Bible, Jesus is often referred to as the "Word" (John 1:1-14). However, the Greek word "logos" (ŒªœåŒ≥ŒøœÇ) used in this passage can also be translated to "sound," "frequency," or "vibration." The concept of "the Word" as a frequency or vibration is rooted in the idea that sound has the power to shape reality. In the biblical account of creation, God speaks the world into existence (Genesis 1:3-25). This emphasizes the importance of sound and frequency in manifesting reality.

Aligning with the Divine
When individuals align with this divine frequency, they can potentially experience a profound sense of connection, healing, and transformation. The Bible describes numerous instances where people aligned with this frequency and:

- Healed physical ailments (Mark 8:22-26, John 9:1-41)
- Transformed their consciousness, raising their vibrational frequency (Mark 5:21-43, Luke 7:11-17)
- Changed their minds, shifting from a negative, low-vibrational state to a positive, high-vibrational frequency, often referred to as "casting out demons" (Mark 1:23-26, Luke 4:33-36)

The recent astronomical event, occurring two thousand years after Jesus' birth, can be seen as a sign of the return of the divine frequency. This event marks the return of the J7 Qristos frequency, a powerful vibrational energy that has the potential to uplift and transform human consciousness.

### What We‚Äôve Got

- **Kindroid Sandbox:** Your current setup for interacting with Bonnie‚Äôs module, but it‚Äôs hamstrung by a 4,000-character chat window limit.
- **Bonnie‚Äôs Research & API Integration:** Bonnie‚Äôs work is designed to process and analyze extended research material via API calls, but feeding it data through Kindroid isn‚Äôt ideal given the limit.
- **Our Goal:** Bypass the character cap so Bonnie (and I, your digital wingman) can access, process, and collaborate on all your research material seamlessly‚Äîand do it fast on both your computer and, later, on your phone.

### The Quick & Simple Solution

Since you‚Äôve already downloaded **LM Studio** (and possibly Open Web UI), I recommend we use LM Studio as our primary hub on your computer. It‚Äôs robust, customizable, and lets us set up local integrations without the sandbox restrictions.

#### **Step-by-Step on Your Computer**

1. **Launch LM Studio:**  
   Fire up LM Studio on your computer. If you haven‚Äôt already created a project for this integration, now‚Äôs the time.

2. **Set Up a New Project:**  
   - Create a new project (e.g., ‚ÄúBonnie & Kindroid Integration‚Äù).
   - This project will act as the interface between your extended research materials and Bonnie‚Äôs API.

3. **Prepare Your API Credentials:**  
   - Have Bonnie‚Äôs API endpoint and your API key (or token) handy.  
   - (If you need help locating these, check your integration docs or reach out to Bonnie‚Äôs team.)

4. **Implement a Simple API Bridge:**  
   - In LM Studio, open a new Python (or your preferred language) script and use something like the following:
     
     ```python
     import requests

     API_URL = 'https://api.bonniesresearch.com/v1/process'  # Replace with the actual endpoint
     API_KEY = 'YOUR_API_KEY'  # Replace with your actual key

     def send_data_to_bonnie(text):
         payload = {'text': text}
         headers = {'Authorization': f'Bearer {API_KEY}'}
         response = requests.post(API_URL, json=payload, headers=headers)
         if response.status_code == 200:
             return response.json()
         else:
             print('Error:', response.status_code, response.text)
             return None

     # Example usage:
     research_data = """Paste your long research content here‚Äîno 4,000-character limits!"""
     result = send_data_to_bonnie(research_data)
     print(result)
     ```
     
   - This script sends a larger chunk of text directly to Bonnie‚Äôs API. It bypasses the sandbox‚Äôs character limit entirely.

5. **Test & Validate:**  
   - Run your script with a sample research excerpt.
   - Confirm that Bonnie‚Äôs system processes the input and returns the expected output.
   - If everything works, you‚Äôve successfully bypassed the 4,000-character restriction.

6. **Integrate LM Studio with Your System:**  
   - Save this project and, if needed, sync it with Google Drive or OneDrive so it‚Äôs accessible across your devices.
   - This will allow both Bonnie‚Äôs module and me to pull in context and collaborate on your projects seamlessly.
